; <L>412<pc>012,1<k1>aDikAra<k2>aDikAra
; old: {%offrande%}
; new: {%<fr>offrande</fr>%}

1655 old {@adhikāra@}¦, <lex>m.</lex>, (= <lang>Pali</lang> <ab>id.</ab>), {%service, respectful duty performed towards another%}, usually a superior (and <ab>esp.</ab> a Buddha); <ls>Senart</ls> <ls>Mv</ls> 〔i.402〕, note on 〔i.37.11—12〕, renders {%offrande%}, and so <ls>Suzuki</ls> on <ls>Laṅk</ls> 〔6.3〕 {%offerings%}. No doubt the ‘service’ often included or consisted of offerings; but that this was not necessarily so is proved by <ls>SP</ls> 〔111.12〕 bahūhi kāryehi kṛtādhikārāḥ, said of merchants (vāṇijāḥ) employed by a wealthy capitalist who {%do service%} (to him) {%with many business-operations%} (certainly not {%offerings%}, kāryehi!). The <ab>cpd.</ab> {@kṛtādhikāra@} (<lang>Pali</lang> katā°) is very common and in <lang>BHS</lang> most often refers to {%services%} performed for present or past Buddhas: <ls>SP</ls> 〔49.13〕; <ls>Laṅk</ls> 〔6.3〕 (kṛtādhikārā buddheṣu kariṣyanty adhunā ca vai); <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.288.8〕; 〔iii.263.12〕; purima-jina-kṛtādhikāra <ls>LV</ls> 〔393.6〕; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.312.5〕; sumahantā adhikārā mayā kṛtā (to former Buddhas) <ls>Mv</ls> 〔iii.241.12〕; (bhagavato …) adhikāraṃ kartuṃ <ls>Mv</ls> 〔i.37.12〕; … kṛtvā <ls>Mv</ls> 〔i.44.14〕; prasannādhikāra, {%service tendered by one who is kindly disposed%}, <ab>i.e.</ab> {%service of friendship%}, <ls>Divy</ls> 〔305.7〕; 〔308.20 ff.〕
;
1655 new {@adhikāra@}¦, <lex>m.</lex>, (= <lang>Pali</lang> <ab>id.</ab>), {%service, respectful duty performed towards another%}, usually a superior (and <ab>esp.</ab> a Buddha); <ls>Senart</ls> <ls>Mv</ls> 〔i.402〕, note on 〔i.37.11—12〕, renders {%<fr>offrande</fr>%}, and so <ls>Suzuki</ls> on <ls>Laṅk</ls> 〔6.3〕 {%offerings%}. 1687 old {@adhitiṣṭhati@}¦, also {@adhiṣṭhahati, °ṣṭhihati@} (and noun {@adhiṣṭhāna@}, <ab>q.v.</ab>; <lang>Pali</lang> adhitiṭṭhati, adhiṭṭhāna, in general in same meanings; previous translations of <lang>BHS</lang> vary widely and are hardly worth systematic quotation; very common is {%bless%}, which I think should be deleted, see below): ({@1@}) {%masters, controls%}, in normal <lang>Skt.</lang> (<ls>BR</ls> sthā with adhi 3, 4) and also <lang>BHS</lang> (<ab>exx.</ab> <ls>LaVallée Poussin, AbhidhK.</ls> 〔vii.119 note 2, b〕); in <lang>BHS</lang> particularly {%takes possession%} or {%control of%}, <ls>MSV</ls> 〔i.248.20〕 (sāptāhikaṃ), and <ab>ff.</ab>; <ls>Bhīk</ls> 〔15a.1〕 (the newly initiated nun says to her instructress) samanvāhara upādhyāyike, aham … idaṃ cīvaraṃ saṃghāṭīm adhitiṣṭhāmi, {%I take%} (formal) {%possession of my nunʼs garments%} (similarly with other implements, below: <ls>Ridding</ls> 〔p. 124〕 calls this rite {%benediction%} of the garments, <ab>etc.</ab>; but the nun is the only speaker; she would not ‘bless’ her own belongings!); in <lang>BHS</lang> ({@2@}) the power or control is usually {%supernatural%} or {%magical%}: adhitiṣṭhantu buddhā bhagavanto idaṃ paṭasūtram <ls>Mmk</ls> 〔56.12〕, {%let the Lord Buddhas exercize their supernatural power over%} (assume control of) {%this thread%} (<ls>Lalou, Iconographie</ls> 〔p. 20〕, {%occupent%}); in the sequel, favorable sounds show the performer that, adhiṣṭhitaṃ me buddhair … tat paṭasūtraṃ (17); he reflects, buddhānāṃ … adhiṣṭhānam etat (24), {%this is the controlling power of the <ab>B.</ab>%}; <ls>Laṅk</ls> 〔100.6 ff.〕 [Page013-a], Bodhisattvas may be adhiṣṭhānadvayādhiṣṭhitāḥ, {%controlled by two supernatural powers%} (of Buddhas, <ab>cf.</ab> 11 buddhādhiṣṭhānādhiṣṭhitāḥ); these are (9) samādhisamāpattyadhiṣṭhāna; {%the control that gives attainment of samādhis%} (<ab>cf.</ab> 12 samādhiṃ samāpadyante; to this verb {@samāpatti@}, <ab>q.v.</ab>, is merely a noun of action; wrongly <ls>Suzuki</ls>), and sarvakāyamukhapāṇyabhiṣekādhiṣṭhāna, {%the control that comes from sprinkling by%} (the Buddhaʼs) {%hands of the whole body and face%} (<ab>cf.</ab> 〔101.10—11〕); persons are said to be adhiṣṭhita, {%supernaturally controlled%} by Buddhas (may often be rendered {%inspired%}) <ls>SP</ls> 〔231.1〕; 〔238.2〕; 〔420.4〕; <ls>LV</ls> 〔275.2〕; <ls>Laṅk</ls> 〔4.13〕; <ab>cf.</ab> {@adhiṣṭhāna@}; this {%control%} often involves ({@3@}) {%magic transformation%}, and even the {%creation of magic appearances%}; not easily separated from the preceding; transitional is sarvabuddhādhiṣṭhito 'yaṃ … dharmaparyāyaḥ <ls>SP</ls> 〔288.13〕, {%it is under the supernatural control of all the Buddhas%} (hence marvelous effects for one who preaches it, as related above), with this <ab>cf.</ab> tasmāt tarhi … adhitiṣṭhāmīmaṃ dharmaparyāyaṃ asmiñ jambudvīpe <ls>SP</ls> 〔421.2〕, {%therefore I%} (<ab>lit.</ab> {%exercize supernatural power over this <ab n="Dharmaparyāya">Dh.</ab>%}, which however here seems to mean) {%make this <ab n="Dharmaparyāya">Dh.</ab> appear in this <ab n="Jambudvīpa">J.</ab>%} (with magical effects, some mentioned above, some in the next sentence); from such passages as this and <ls>SP</ls> 〔384.3〕, below, <ls>LaVallée Poussin, AbhidhK.</ls>, 〔Index〕, and <ab>esp.</ab> 〔vii.119, note 2〕, derives the supposed meaning {%<fr>faire durer</fr>%}, but in 〔iii.31〕, note 2, quoting the vyākhyā, he translates adhitiṣṭhati {%<fr>bénit</fr>%}, whereas it means {%takes under control, assumes control of%}; the meaning {%bless%}, assumed by <ls>Burnouf</ls> and many others, rests on <lang>Tib.</lang> <tib>byin kyi rlabs</tib>, which to be sure often means {%bless%}, but <ab>acc.</ab> to <ls>Jäschke</ls> also {%create, change into%}; this kind of change by magical mastery or control need not be a {%blessing%}, <ab>cf.</ab> (tā jarājarjarā) adhyatiṣṭhat <ls>LV</ls> 〔378.17〕, {%he changed them%} (the daughters of Māra, by magic control) {%so as to be decrepit with age%}, and later, buddhasya yo hy adhiṣṭhānaṃ śaknuyāt kartum anyathā 〔379.3〕, (I see no one) {%who could alter a magic transformation of the Buddha%}; mahābrahmā imaṃ … lokadhātuṃ tat kṣaṇaṃ samam adhyatiṣṭhat, pāṇitalajātam … tṛṇair imaṃ … lokadhātuṃ saṃchāditam adhyatiṣṭhat <ls>LV</ls> 〔276.19 ff.〕, {%the Great Brahmā magically mastered%} (and thereby changed) {%this entire world%} (so as to be) {%even%}, <ab>etc.</ab>, {%… covered with grass%}; in <ls>SP</ls> 〔384.3〕 (as he was about to die, Sadāparibhūta heard this sūtra; then, not dying after all,) adhiṣṭhihitvā ca sudīrgham āyuḥ, {%and having mastered, acquired, assumed by magic, very long life%} (he proceeded to proclaim this sūtra; similar passages are taken by <ls>LaVallée Poussin</ls> <ab>l. c.</ab> to mean {%faire durer%}); (Bhagavān …) jīvitasaṃskārān adhiṣṭhāya āyuḥsaṃskārān utsraṣṭum ārabdhaḥ. samanantarādhiṣṭhiteṣu jīvitasaṃskāreṣu (omens occurred) <ls>Divy</ls> 〔203.7—8〕 (in this phrase <ls>LaV-P, AbhidhK.</ls> 〔ii.122〕. renders {%<fr>stabilisé</fr>%}; note the term vaśitva in the <ab>comm.</ab>, <ab>l. c.</ab> 〔124 line 1〕; render {%controlling%}), see {@saṃskāra@} 2; buddhā bhagavantaḥ taṃ pṛthivīpradeśaṃ vajramayam adhitiṣṭhanti sma <ls>LV</ls> 〔86.16—17〕, {%… magically made this spot of ground%} (where the young Bodhisattva took seven steps) {%hard as a diamond%}, so that it did not sink under his feet (<ab>N.B.</ab> they did not literally {%stand upon%} it; they were located sthitāḥ line 16, in the ten quarters); tatrāpi cātmānam adhiṣṭhahāmi, sarvāṃś ca sattvān ah[am] adhiṣṭhihāmi (so read, 〔§ 8.99〕) <ls>SP</ls> 〔323.13〕, {%there%} (having made it appear that I entered nirvāṇa, <ab>tho</ab> I did not) {%I make myself appear%} (create myself magically, <ab>cf.</ab> 〔316.1〕, <ab>s.v.</ab> adhiṣṭhāna 3), {%and I control all creatures%} (in next line, {%men of perverted minds were deluded and did not see me, <ab>tho</ab> I was standing right there%}); with <ls>SP</ls> 〔384.3〕 <ab>cf.</ab> <ls>Dbh</ls> 〔91.28〕 sarvasattvāṃś ca ākāṅkṣan yathābhiprāyaṃ rūpāśrayālaṃkṛtān adhitiṣṭhati; in this section adhitiṣṭhati occurs many times, beginning with 〔90.21—22〕 saṃkṣiptāyā lokadhātor vistīrṇatām adhitiṣṭhati, and means always (a Bodhisattva in the tenth stage) {%makes appear magically%}, either by transformation or creation; <ab>cf.</ab> in <lang>Pali</lang> <ls>Therag.</ls> 〔1131〕 [Page013-b] satthā ca me lokam imaṃ adhiṭṭhahi (<lex>aor.</lex>) aniccato {%… the Teacher made this world appear to me as impermanent%} (by his supernatural power, but this time without the usual connotation of magic or illusion); catvāri pātrāṇi pratigṛhyaikaṃ pātram adhitiṣṭheyam <ls>LV</ls> 〔384.4—5〕, {%accepting the four bowls I will change them magically into a single bowl%}, which he does; pratigṛhya caikaṃ pātram adhitiṣṭhati sma, adhimuktibalena 〔385.4〕 (see {@adhimukti@} 2 which in such passages = adhiṣṭhāna).

; <L>434<pc>014,1<k1>aDimukti<k2>aDimukti
; old: {%croyance%}
; new: {%<fr>croyance</fr>%}
; -----
1743 old {@adhimukti@}¦, <lex>f.</lex> (= <lang>Pali</lang> adhimutti; to {@adhimucyate@}), ({@1@}) {%strong inclination, attachment; earnest, zealous application%}; <lang>Tib.</lang> <tib>mos pa</tib> (<ls>Jäschke</ls>, {%to be pleased%}, <tib>la</tib> {%with; to wish, to have a mind; to take pleasure in, to rejoice at%}; as substantive {%pleasure, satisfaction, esteem%}; also {%to respect, to esteem, to respect with devotion, to revere, to adore%}); <ls>LaV-P. AbhidhK. Index</ls> = ruci; <ab>cf.</ab> <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔95.12—13〕 kathaṃ ca bodhisattvo 'dhimuktibahulo bhavati? iha bodhisattvo 'ṣṭavidhe 'dhimuktyadhiṣṭhāne śraddhāprasādapūrvakeṇa niścayena {%rucyā%} samanvāgato bhavati. (Other alleged meanings, as {%croyance%} <ls>Lévi Sūtrāl.</ls> 〔i.13 note 1〕; {%confiance%}, <ls>Burnouf</ls>; {%good will%}, <ls>Kern</ls>, in translation of <ls>SP</ls>; <ab>etc.</ab>, are not supported by <lang>BHS</lang> usage, except as under 2, below.) It may be (but rarely is) applied to (a) non-religious objects: sa ca puruṣas (the father) teṣāṃ kumārakāṇām (his ignorant sons) āśayajño bhaved, adhimuktiṃ ca vijānīyāt, <ls>SP</ls> 〔73.14—15〕, {%… and he understands their inclinations, what they are interested in%}. But usually the object is related to (b) a religious aim. It may be specified, syntactically (in the <lex>loc.</lex>), as in yaṃ … sugataḥ prabhāṣate, adhimuktisaṃpanna bhavāhi tatra <ls>SP</ls> 〔32.15〕, {%what the Buddha says, be perfect in zealous application to that%}. Usually it is not so specifically stated, <ab>tho</ab> the context is apt to suggest that it is {%zealous cultivation%} (study or propagation) of sacred texts or religious instruction that is meant (note-that the object of the verb {@adhimucyate@} is commonly something of this sort); <ab>cf.</ab> <ab>e.g.</ab> -lokaṃ yathādhimuktyā ({%according to their%} [varying types or degrees of] {%zeal or application%}) subhāṣitena saṃtoṣayantam <ls>LV</ls> 〔160.17〕; adhimuktisāro yo syād … saḥ, puṇyaṃ labheta yo etaṃ (most <ab>mss.</ab>) sūtraṃ vācel likheta vā <ls>SP</ls> 〔342.3—4〕. And this is probably meant as a rule when the context gives no special clue, as in many of the following: <ls>SP</ls> 〔6.13〕; 〔31.6〕; 〔93.9〕; 〔125.8〕; 〔235.10〕; 〔274.10〕; <ls>LV</ls> 〔10.11〕; 〔182.20〕; 〔432.8〕; <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔856〕; <ls>Samādh</ls> 〔22.43〕; <ls>RP</ls> 〔20.5〕; <ls>Bhad</ls> 〔7, 48〕; <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔195.12〕; anadhimukti, {%lack of%} (religious) {%zeal%} <ls>RP</ls> 〔19.18〕; 〔35.4〕; various gods in <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.309.14 ff.〕 see the bodhi-tree svakāye adhmuktīye, {%according to their tastes, inclinations, interests%} (<ls>Senart</ls> {%<fr>suivant ľinclination de chacun</fr>%}) as made of various [Page014-b] precious materials; one of the ten bala of a tathāgata is nānādhimuktijñānabala <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔122〕 (and <ab>cf.</ab> <ls>Mv</ls> 〔i.159.15〕 adhimuktinānātvaṃ vetti, as one of the ten bala); adhimuktivaśitā <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔776〕, one of the 10 vaśitā of a Bodhisattva; yathādhimuktyā, <lex>adv.</lex>, <ls>LV</ls> 〔160.17〕 (above) and 〔179.17〕; hīnādhimukti, {%attachment to low ends%}, <ls>SP</ls> 〔115.12〕 (<ab>cf.</ab> hīnādhimukta, °tika, <ab>s.vv.</ab> {@adhimukta, °tika@}); (in <ls>LV</ls> 〔294.4〕 for vidyādhimuktiprabhaḥ read probably vidyāvimukti°, {%having the splendor of%} (true) {%knowledge and emancipation%}, so <lang>Tib.</lang>, <tib>rnam par grol ba</tib> = vimukti); ({@2@}) {%magic transformation%}, in adhimukti-balena <ls>LV</ls> 〔385.5〕, see <ab>s.v.</ab> {@adhimucyate@} (2), and {@adhitiṣṭhati@}, end.
;

AbhidhK. Index</ls> = ruci; <ab>cf.</ab> <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔95.12—13〕 kathaṃ ca bodhisattvo 'dhimuktibahulo bhavati? iha bodhisattvo 'ṣṭavidhe 'dhimuktyadhiṣṭhāne śraddhāprasādapūrvakeṇa niścayena {%rucyā%} samanvāgato bhavati. ;24169 old {@caṅkrama@}¦, <lex>m.</lex> and (less regularly) <lex>nt.</lex> (= <lang>Pali</lang> caṅkama; to {@caṅkramati@}), ({@1@}) {%act of walking%}, in purely physical sense: vivṛtaḥ śobhate ārya āsana-sthāna-caṅkrame <ls>LV</ls> 〔157.15〕 (<ab>vs</ab>), {%when uncovered%} (unveiled), {%a noble person shines%} (is distinguished) {%in sitting, standing, and walking%}; these are three of the (usually four) modes of physical behavior (the fourth being lying down), see <ab>s.v.</ab> {@īryāpatha@} 4; <ls>AsP</ls> 〔520.13〕; <ls>RP</ls> 〔45.18〕; cognate <lex>acc.</lex> °maṃ caṅkramyate or °mati, see (4) below; ({@2@}) {%walking, wandering%}, as an occupation or mode of life: in <ls>Karmav</ls> 〔104.14〕 one of the daśa guṇāḥ paiṇḍapātikatve, {%ten advantages in the mendicantʼs life%}, is, caṅkramo 'sya upārjito bhavati, {%he has acquired%} (a life of) {%walking, wandering about%}; ({@3@}) {%place of walking, promenade%} (in the sense of {%ground where walking is done%}): of walks in groves or parks (secular), ekaikaṃ caṅkrama-varaṃ … kalpayatha <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.18.16〕 (<ab>vs</ab>), Śuddhodana says, {%adorn%} (or with <ab>mss.</ab> kalpayama, {%let us adorn%}) {%every excellent promenade%} (in the Lumbinī grove, in preparation for Māyāʼs visit); gṛha-dhana-dhānyaśayana-vasanaṃ caṅkramodyānāni cānekaśo yācanakebhyo nisṛṣṭāni <ls>LV</ls> 〔318.5〕 (prose), {%… promenades and parks were bestowed on beggars many times%}; ({@4@}) especially, {%promenade, terrace, place for walking%} (often rendered {%cloister%}), for monks or Buddhas or other ascetics; sometimes associated with places for ‘standing, sitting, lying down’, the other {@īryāpatha@}, see <ab>mg.</ab> (1) above: samyaksaṃbuddhānāṃ adhiṣṭhitāni caṅkramā niṣadyāni śayyāni <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.163.18〕; so frequently abhi-ruh- occurs in <lang>BHS</lang> with this word): araṇyavāsi (<lex>loc.</lex>; <ab>v.l.</ab> °se) tiṣṭhanto caṅkrame (<ls>WT</ls> °mam with <ms>Ḱ</ms>) abhiruhya ca <ls>SP</ls> 〔335.5〕 (<ab>vs</ab>); ārāmāś caṅkramā dattāḥ (to Buddha and his monks) 〔341.13〕 (<ab>vs</ab>); ye keci bhikṣū sugatasya śāsane, abhiyuktarūpā sthita caṅkrameṣu 〔365.5〕 (<ab>vs</ab>); (yasmiṃś ca … grāme vā nagare vā …) janapadapradeśe vā caṅkrame vā vihāre vā ayaṃ Lalitavistaro … pracariṣyati <ls>LV</ls> 〔442.11〕; {%the long%} (-continued) {%promenade%} (<ab>cf.</ab> <ls>Mv</ls> 〔iii.114.12—13〕 above) seems to have been a special spiritual exercise, to which exceptional importance is attached, and the cognate <lex>accus.</lex> in the following may be partly a noun of action, <ab>tho</ab> it seems rarely if ever completely separate from the place-designation; the Buddha, in the 2d or 3d week after enlightenment, (dvitīye) saptāhe tathāgato dīrghacaṅkramaṃ caṅkramyate sma <ls>LV</ls> 〔377.4〕, (tṛtīyaṃ) saptāhaṃ prītisukhena dīrghaṃ caṅkramaṃ caṅkrame (<lex>aor.</lex>) <ls>Mv</ls> 〔iii.281.12〕; (Buddha, vihārāto nirgamya … smitaṃ prāduṣkaritvā) dīrghaṃ caṅkramaṃ caṅkrame (<lex>aor.</lex>) <ls>Mv</ls> 〔i.317.(7—)9〕; without use of the word dīrgha, the like is presented in <ls>SP</ls>, with emphasis on spiritual results: (the Bodhisattva Sarvasattvapriyadarśana) dvādaśa varṣasahasrāṇi caṅkramābhirūḍho (<lang>Tib.</lang> <tib>ḥchag pa la zhugs śiṅ</tib>, {%having begun, undertaken, a walk%}) 'bhūn mahāvīryārambheṇa yogābhiyukto 'bhūt <ls>SP</ls> 〔405.13〕, followed by reference to this in 〔408.14〕 (<ab>vs</ab>), spoken by the Bodhisattva <ab n="Sarvasattvapriyadarśana">S.</ab>, ayaṃ mamā caṅkrama rāja śreṣṭha yasmin mayā sthitva samādhi labdhaḥ; similarly, yadā ca sa dharmabhāṇako 'smin dharmaparyāye cintāyogam anuyuktaś caṅkramābhirūḍho bhaviṣyati, tadāhaṃ … tasya dharmabhāṇakasya caṅkrama-kuṭīm (<lang>Tib.</lang> <tib>ḥchag paḥi</tib>, = caṅkrama, <tib>gnas</tib>, = {%place%}, <ab>esp.</ab> {%abode, habitation%}; in the outside world, what is hollow and empty (as a hole in the ground); vijñānadhātu 〔250.5 ff.〕, (line 7) ṣaḍindriyādhipateyā (see {@ādhipateya@}) ṣaḍviṣayārambaṇā (read °baṇa-, in accord with line 5 cakṣurindriyādhipateyā rūpārambaṇaprativijñaptiḥ; these four only make up the several senses; ākāśa, {%emptiness%}, cannot be involved, and vijñāna (six-fold) is what results from the operation of each sense on its appropriate objects; ({@2@}) {%element%} in the body exclusively and specifically (aside from 1 above [Page283-a] which applies to the body but also to all the external world), pretty much as in <lang>Skt.</lang> (<ls>BR</ls> <ab>s.v.</ab> dhātu 3), but I have found no numerical listing of them in <lang>BHS</lang> (in <lang>Skt.</lang> various numbers occur, rarely 3 = the 3 doṣa, {%wind, gall, phlegm%}; but regularly 7, sometimes 5 or 10), {%main constituent%} of the body: in <ls>Suv</ls> 〔179.5〕 six (ṣaḍdhātu-kauśalya, see below, end, note*); abhiṣyaṇṇā vātātapā saṃvṛttā <ls>Mv</ls> 〔iii.143.16〕, <ab>cf.</ab> abhiṣyaṇṇehi dhātūhi 〔144.6〕; 〔153.11〕; 〔154.8〕, see <ab>s.vv.</ab> {@abhiṣyaṇṇa@} and {@vātātapa@}, {%excessive%} or {%over-exuberant bodily humors%} (a cause of disease; <lang>Pali</lang> uses abhi(s)sanna of the dosa, <lang>Skt.</lang> doṣa, [three] bodily humors); dhātuvaiṣamyāc ca glānaḥ <ls>Divy</ls> 〔191.28〕, {%sick from an upset condition of the humors%}; tvaṃ vaidya (<ab>n. sg.</ab>; so divide) dhātukuśalas <ls>LV</ls> 〔184.21〕 (<ab>vs</ab>), {%thou, a physician skilled in the humors%} or {%bodily elements%}; kaccid dhātavaḥ pratikurvanti <ls>SP</ls> 〔429.4〕, {%I hope your bodily humors%} (or {%elements%}) {%are acting properly?%}; ({@3@}) the 18 dhātu, {%psycho-physical constituent elements%} of the personality in relation to the outside world (<lang>Pali</lang> <ab>id.</ab>), are the 12 {@āyatana@} (<ab>i.e.</ab> the 6 senses plus 6 sense-objects, see <ab>s.v.</ab> 5) plus the 6 corresponding sensory perceptions, {@vijñāna@}; listed <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔2040—58〕, cakṣur-dhātuḥ, rūpa-dhātuḥ, cakṣur-vijñāna-dhātuḥ, and so with śrotra (śabda), ghrāṇa (gandha), jihvā (rasa), kāya (spraṣṭavya), mano (dharma); same in abbreviated form (with sparśa for spraṣṭavya) <ls>Dharmas</ls> 〔25〕; in this sense I understand nānādhātu-jñāna-balam <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔123〕 (one of the 10 balāni of a Buddha), and (also one of the 10 balāni) nānādhātukaṃ (-ka <ab>Bhvr.</ab>; = °dhātuṃ) lokaṃ vidanti <ls>Mv</ls> 〔i.159.14〕; note ākāśadhātu alone <ls>SP</ls> 〔253.13〕; 〔342.11〕) and also vijñāna (<lang>Pali</lang> viññāṇa), listed <ls>Dharmas</ls> 〔58〕 as ṣaḍ dhātavaḥ; important is <ls>Śikṣ</ls> 〔244.11 ff.〕 (similarly <ls>Bcṭ</ls> 〔326.24 ff.〕): ṣaḍdhātur ayaṃ … puruṣaḥ … katame ṣaṭ? tad yathā: pṛthivīdhātur abdh° tejodh° vāyudh° ākāśadh° vijñānadh° ca … ṣaḍ imāni … SParśāyatanāni (see {@āyatana@} 5) … cakṣuḥ sparśāyatanaṃ rūpāṇāṃ darśanāya, (and so) śrotraṃ … ghrāṇaṃ … jihvā … kāya(ḥ) sparśāyatanaṃ spraṣṭavyānāṃ sparśanāya, manaḥ spa° dharmāṇāṃ vijñānāya … (〔245.1 ff.〕) adhyātmikaḥ pṛthivīdhātuḥ, which is whatever is {%hard%} in the body, as hair, nails, teeth, <ab>etc.</ab>; (〔245.4〕) bāhyaḥ pṛthivīdhātuḥ is whatever is {%hard%} in the outside world. Similarly with abdhātu 〔246.16 ff.〕; tejodhātu 〔248.2 ff.〕; vāyudhātu 〔248.11—249.3〕; ākāśadhātu 〔249.3 ff.〕, in the body of man, is such things as the mouth, throat, <ab>etc.</ab> ({%empty space%}, we would say); in the outside world, what is hollow and empty (as a hole in the ground); vijñānadhātu 〔250.5 ff.〕, (line 7) ṣaḍindriyādhipateyā (see {@ādhipateya@}) ṣaḍviṣayārambaṇā (read °baṇa-, in accord with line 5 cakṣurindriyādhipateyā rūpārambaṇaprativijñaptiḥ; see {@ārambaṇa@} 3) viṣayavijñaptir ayam ucyate vijñānadhātuḥ (this is only adhyātmika; there is no external vijñāna); in 〔250.14 ff.〕 it is made clear that the sparśāyatanāni, <ab>i.e.</ab> the sensory organs or powers (〔244.15 ff.〕), are constituted by {%equilibrium%} or {%tranquillity%} ({@prasāda@} 2, <ab>q.v.</ab>) of the four physical elements (a, above, here called mahābhūtāni, as in <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔1837〕): katamac cakṣurāyatanam? yac caturṇāṃ mahābhūtānāṃ prasādaḥ, tad yathā, pṛthivīdhātor abdhātos tejodhātor vāyudhātor yāvat, <ab>etc.</ab>; these four only make up the several senses; ākāśa, {%emptiness%}, cannot be involved, and vijñāna (six-fold) is what results from the operation of each sense on its appropriate objects; ({@2@}) {%element%} in the body exclusively and specifically (aside from 1 above [Page283-a] which applies to the body but also to all the external world), pretty much as in <lang>Skt.</lang> (<ls>BR</ls> <ab>s.v.</ab> dhātu 3), but I have found no numerical listing of them in <lang>BHS</lang> (in <lang>Skt.</lang> various numbers occur, rarely 3 = the 3 doṣa, {%wind, gall, phlegm%}; but regularly 7, sometimes 5 or 10), {%main constituent%} of the body: in <ls>Suv</ls> 〔179.5〕 six (ṣaḍdhātu-kauśalya, see below, end, note*); abhiṣyaṇṇā vātātapā saṃvṛttā <ls>Mv</ls> 〔iii.143.16〕, <ab>cf.</ab> abhiṣyaṇṇehi dhātūhi 〔144.6〕; 〔153.11〕; 〔154.8〕, see <ab>s.vv.</ab> {@abhiṣyaṇṇa@} and {@vātātapa@}, {%excessive%} or {%over-exuberant bodily humors%} (a cause of disease; <lang>Pali</lang> uses abhi(s)sanna of the dosa, <lang>Skt.</lang> doṣa, [three] bodily humors); dhātuvaiṣamyāc ca glānaḥ <ls>Divy</ls> 〔191.28〕, {%sick from an upset condition of the humors%}; tvaṃ vaidya (<ab>n. sg.</ab>; so divide) dhātukuśalas <ls>LV</ls> 〔184.21〕 (<ab>vs</ab>), {%thou, a physician skilled in the humors%} or {%bodily elements%}; kaccid dhātavaḥ pratikurvanti <ls>SP</ls> 〔429.4〕, {%I hope your bodily humors%} (or {%elements%}) {%are acting properly?%}; ({@3@}) the 18 dhātu, {%psycho-physical constituent elements%} of the personality in relation to the outside world (<lang>Pali</lang> <ab>id.</ab>), are the 12 {@āyatana@} (<ab>i.e.</ab> the 6 senses plus 6 sense-objects, see <ab>s.v.</ab> 5) plus the 6 corresponding sensory perceptions, {@vijñāna@}; listed <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔2040—58〕, cakṣur-dhātuḥ, rūpa-dhātuḥ, cakṣur-vijñāna-dhātuḥ, and so with śrotra (śabda), ghrāṇa (gandha), jihvā (rasa), kāya (spraṣṭavya), mano (dharma); same in abbreviated form (with sparśa for spraṣṭavya) <ls>Dharmas</ls> 〔25〕; aṣṭādaśa dhātavaś <ls>LV</ls> 〔372.7〕; see also {@varṇa-dhātu@}; ({@4@}) {%constituent element%} of the mind, ‘heart’, or character, and so by extension (psychic) {%character, nature, natural disposition%}; as {%element%} of the citta, <ls>Av</ls> 〔ii.140.13 ff.〕, śamatha-vipaśyanā-paribhāvitam … (14) āryaśrāvakasya cittaṃ dhātuśo (<ab>cf.</ab> <lang>Pali</lang> dhātuso in quite similar sense, <ls>SN</ls> 〔ii.154.19 ff.〕, referring to dhātu 〔153.23 ff.〕; note avijjā-dhātu 〔153.29〕) vimucyate. tatra sthavira katame dhātavaḥ? yaś ca … (〔141.1〕) prahāṇa-dhātur yaś ca virāga-dhātur yaś ca nirodha-dhātuḥ, kasya nu … prahāṇāt (2) prahāṇadhātur ity ucyate? … (3) sarvasaṃskārāṇāṃ … prahāṇāt prahāṇadhātur ity ucyate, and so identically with virāga and nirodha; in this sense I understand nānādhātu-jñāna-balam <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔123〕 (one of the 10 balāni of a Buddha), and (also one of the 10 balāni) nānādhātukaṃ (-ka <ab>Bhvr.</ab>; = °dhātuṃ) lokaṃ vidanti <ls>Mv</ls> 〔i.159.14〕; nānādhātum imaṃ lokam anuvartanti paṇḍitāḥ (= Tathāgatāḥ) <ls>Mv</ls> 〔i.90.17〕; <lang>Pali</lang> similarly has anekadhātu and nānādhātu as <ab>eps.</ab> of loka, and knowledge of them as one of the 10 balāni, <ab>e.g.</ab> <ls>MN</ls> 〔i.70.9—10〕, where <ab>comm.</ab> 〔ii.29.20 ff.〕 is uncertain, cakkhudhātu-ādīhi (see 3 above) kāmadhātu-ādīhi (see 5 below) vā dhātūhi bahudhātuṃ … lokaṃ ti khandhāyatanadhātu-lokaṃ (see below); but <ls>DN</ls> 〔ii.282.25 ff.〕 seems to prove that the <ab>mg.</ab> is different, anekadhātu nānādhātu kho … loko …, yaṃ yad eva sattā dhātuṃ abhinivisanti, taṃ tad eva thāmasā … abhinivissa voharanti: idam eva saccaṃ moghaṃ aññaṃ ti; tasmā na sabbe … ekantavādā ekantasīlā ekantachandā ekanta-ajjhosānā ti (here, dhātu is surely something like {%nature, disposition%}, as <ab>comm.</ab> says, ajjhāsaya, 〔iii.737.18〕); similarly, nānādhimuktānāṃ sattvānāṃ nānādhātv-āśayānām āśayaṃ viditvā <ls>SP</ls> 〔41.3〕; 〔71.8〕, {%knowing the disposition of creatures who vary in interests and who vary in character and disposition%}; <ls>CPD</ls> <ab>s.v.</ab> anekadhātu (as <ab>ep.</ab> of loka) is not quite clear, saying {%with many elements, or natural conditions (or dispositions)%}; confirmation of this interpretation may be found in a cliché, (bhagavāṃs teṣāṃ, or the like) … āśayānuśayaṃ (see {@anuśaya@}) dhātuṃ prakṛtiṃ ca jñātvā (evidently {%disposition, character%}, or {%state of mind%}) <ls>Divy</ls> 〔46.23〕; 〔47.9—10〕; 〔48.12—13〕; 〔49.11—12〕; (in 〔209.12〕 <ab>cpd.</ab> āśayānuśayadhātuprakṛtiṃ ca, in view of ca <ab>prob.</ab> to be read °dhātuṃ;) 〔462.9—10〕; 〔463.18—19〕, <ab>etc.</ab>; <ls>Av</ls> 〔i.64.12—13〕; also āśayasya tava dhātu tādṛśaḥ <ls>Gv</ls> 〔484.16〕, above, and possibly jñāna-dhātu in the same line, but here {%sphere%} (5, below) may be meant; here also, it seems, must be included dhātu, {%state of mind, psychic characteristic%}, when used parallel (or in composition) with [Page283-b] skandha and āyatana (where, if sense 3 were intended, āyatana would be included in dhātu so that tautology would result), as: te skandhā tāni dhātūni tāni āyatanāni ca, ātmānaṃ ca adhikṛtya bhagavān tam (<ab>mss.</ab> etam; <ls>Senart</ls>ʼs <ab>em.</ab> leaves the meter still bad) arthaṃ vyākare (<ab>v.l.</ab> °ret) <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.93.20—21〕 (<ab>vss</ab>); na skandha-āyatanadhātu (read as one dvandva <ab>cpd.</ab>, as suggested by <lang>Tib.</lang> <tib>phuṅ po skye mched khams rnams</tib>, the last syllable being the plural suffix, put after the third noun only, <tib>saṅs rgyas yin mi smra</tib>) vademi Buddhaṃ <ls>LV</ls> 〔420.17〕 (<ab>vs</ab>), {%I do not say that the skandha, sense-organs and their objects, and states of mind are Buddha%}; skandhadhātvāyataneṣu <ls>Divy</ls> 〔54.5 ff.〕 <ab>etc.</ab> (see 1a, above), roughly, {%in the mental%} (not gross-physical) {%constitution%}; in <ls>LV</ls> 〔177.5〕 (<ab>vs</ab>) read, skandhāyatanāni dhātavaḥ, with citation of the line <ls>Śikṣ</ls> 〔240.5〕, as required by meter and supported by <lang>Tib.</lang> (<ls>Lefm.</ls> skandhadhātvāyatanāni dhātavaḥ); 32015 old {@dhyāna@}¦, <lex>nt.</lex> (<lang>Skt.</lang> <ab>id.</ab>; in technical sense = <lang>Pali</lang> jhāna), <ab>lit.</ab> {%meditation%} or {%contemplation; mystic ‘trance’%}; <ls>Lévi (Sūtrāl.)</ls> {%extase%}. Normally {%four%}, as in <lang>Pali</lang>, described in some detail in a long ancient passage (the <lang>Pali</lang> form, virtually identical, cited in <ls>Childers</ls>), found with hardly a true variant <ls>LV</ls> 〔129.1—11〕; 〔343.14—344.4〕; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔i.228.3—10〕; 〔ii.131.16—132.5〕; <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔1478—1481〕; an abbreviated form, giving the central points, as follows: savitarkaṃ savicāraṃ vivekajaṃ prītisukham iti prathamadhyānaṃ, adhyātmapramodanāt [Page287-b] prītisukham iti dvitīyaṃ, upekṣāsmṛtisaṃprajanyaṃ sukham iti tṛtīyaṃ, upekṣāsmṛtipariśuddhir aduḥkhāsukhā vedaneti caturthaṃ dhyānam iti <ls>Dharmas</ls> 〔72〕; they are the first four of the nine {@anupūrvavihāra(-samāpatti)@}, <ab>qq.v.</ab>; these are related to the four dhyānabhūmi constituted or occupied by the various classes of {@rūpāvacara@} gods (see {@deva@}), as explained by <ls>Childers</ls>, in that attainment in worldly life of (various stages of adeptness in) each of the four dhyāna leads to rebirth in successively higher stages among these gods; catu-dhyāna- (meter proves single initial consonant pronounced for written dhy-)-dhyāyino (as before) <ls>SP</ls> 〔131.5〕 (<ab>vs</ab>); {%three%} dhyāna, listed as sadoṣāpakarṣa-, sukhavaihārika-, and aśeṣavaibhūṣita- (read {@°vaibhūtika-?@} see this word), <ls>Dharmas</ls> 〔109〕; I have found no other trace of this list; the names sound vaguely as if the first might apply to the first of the 4 dhyāna, the second to the 2d and 3d combined, and the third to the 4th; in <ls>Laṅk</ls> 〔10.11〕 na ṣaḍdhyānādidhyāyinā (tvayā bhavitavyam), {%you should not meditate on such things as the six dhyāna%}; apparently some reprehended practices are meant, but I have no more idea of the specific meaning than had <ls>Suzuki</ls> (<ls>Studies</ls>, 〔414〕).
;

34637 old {@nītārtha@}¦, <lex>adj.</lex> (<ab>cf.</ab> <ls>BR</ls> <ab>s.v.</ab> nī, 12, {%establish, determine%}; = <lang>Pali</lang> nītattha), {%of clear, definite, well-established meaning%}; <ab>opp.</ab> a-nītārtha or {@neyārtha@}, {%having a meaning that is not%} (clearly) {%established, that has to be determined%} (by inference or the like); see <ls>LaVallée-Poussin, AbhidhK.</ls> 〔ix.246—8〕 for very complete and illuminating discussion of these terms in <lang>Pali</lang> and <lang>BHS</lang>. (In <lang>Pali</lang> neither is ipso facto preferred to the other; one errs only in interpreting one as if it were the other, nītattha as neyyattha, or vice versa; see <ab>esp.</ab> <ls>AN</ls> 〔i.60.13—15〕, and <ab>comm.</ab> 〔ii.118.7—27〕; <ls>Dīpav.</ls> 〔5.34〕, <ls>Oldenberg</ls> 〔p. 36〕, and <ls>LaV-P.</ls> <ab>l. c.</ab>) In <lang>BHS</lang> a nītārtha text, {%de sens explicite%} (<ls>LaV-P.</ls>), is recommended as a guide in preference to one that is neyārtha, <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔1549〕; <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔257.10 ff.〕 Equivalent to neyārtha is a-nītārtha, for which see <ls>LaV-P.</ls> <ab>l. c.</ab> 〔248〕.
;
34637 new {@nītārtha@}¦, <lex>adj.</lex> (<ab>cf.</ab> <ls>BR</ls> <ab>s.v.</ab> nī, 12, {%establish, determine%}; = <lang>Pali</lang> nītattha), {%of clear, definite, well-established meaning%}; <ab>opp.</ab> a-nītārtha or {@neyārtha@}, {%having a meaning that is not%} (clearly) {%established, that has to be determined%} (by inference or the like); see <ls>LaVallée-Poussin, AbhidhK.</ls> 〔ix.246—8〕 for very complete and illuminating discussion of these terms in <lang>Pali</lang> and <lang>BHS</lang>. (In <lang>Pali</lang> neither is ipso facto preferred to the other; one errs only in interpreting one as if it were the other, nītattha as neyyattha, or vice versa; see <ab>esp.</ab> <ls>AN</ls> 〔i.60.13—15〕, and <ab>comm.</ab> 〔ii.118.7—27〕; <ls>Dīpav.</ls> 〔5.34〕, <ls>Oldenberg</ls> 〔p. 36〕, and <ls>LaV-P.</ls> <ab>l. c.</ab>) In <lang>BHS</lang> a nītārtha text, {%<fr>de sens explicite</fr>%} (<ls>LaV-P.</ls>), is recommended as a guide in preference to one that is neyārtha, <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔1549〕; <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔257.10 ff.〕 Equivalent to neyārtha is a-nītārtha, for which see <ls>LaV-P.</ls> <ab>l. c.</ab> 〔248〕.

; <L>8994<pc>322,2<k1>parijaya<k2>parijaya
; old: {%un maître%}
; new: {%<fr>un maître</fr>%}

36107 old {@parijaya@}¦, <lex>m.</lex> (see next; = <lang>Skt.</lang> paricaya, 〔§ 2.28〕, <ab>cf.</ab> <ab>s.vv.</ab> {@paricita, paricetar@}), {%intensive cultivation, thorough acquaintance, familiarity, careful consideration%} (with <lex>loc.</lex>): <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔6532〕; <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔11.16〕 a-parijayād; <ls>AsP</ls> 〔293.1〕 prajñāyāṃ parijayaṃ karoṣi; 〔322.3〕; 〔332.9〕 dhyāna-parijayaṃ ca karoti; 〔356.14〕 ānimitte ca parijayaṃ karoti; 〔370.3〕 śūnyatāyāṃ; 〔370.16, 17〕. Prakritic j for c: Leumann cited by <ls>Wogihara in Bbh. Lex. 32</ls>. According to <ls>Wogihara</ls>, in <ls>AsP</ls> 〔332.9〕 the word would mean {%conquest, mastery%}, from root ji, and also in a <ab>ms.</ab> citation from Yaśomitra, <ls>AbhidhK.</ls> (<ab>cf.</ab> <ls>LaV-P.</ls> 〔vi.150〕) yogācāras trividhaḥ, ādikarmikaḥ, kṛtaparijayaḥ ({%un maître%}, <ls>LaV-P.</ls>), atikrāntamanasikāraś ca. I see no reason to separate these passages from the others. It is clear to me that <lang>BHS</lang> has only one word parijaya, and I think Leumannʼs interpretation is the true one. <lang>Tib.</lang> on <ls>Mvy</ls> <tib>yoṅs su</tib> (= pari) <tib>byaṅ bar</tib> (sometimes {%purification%}, but also <ab>acc.</ab> to <ls>Das</ls> {%skilled%}; also used for {@paricita, °cetar@}, <ab>qq.v.</ab>; note that <ls>Mironov</ls> reads parijita, °jetar for these) <tib>byas pa</tib> ({%made, the making%}), or <tib>ḥdris par</tib> ({%acquaintance%}) <tib>bya ba</tib> ({%making, being made%}). <lang>Chin.</lang> and <lang>Jap.</lang> seem to follow <lang>Tib.</lang>
;

51753 old {@lakṣaṇa@}¦, <lex>nt.</lex>, {%mark%} (<lang>Skt.</lang>); ({@1@}) in <ls>Laṅk</ls> 〔37.10 ff.〕; 〔38.5 ff.〕, {%external mark, manifested aspect%}, of the vijñāna (<ab>cf.</ab> <ls>Suzuki, Studies</ls>, 〔183〕); contrasted with {@prabandha@}, <ab>q.v.</ab>; fuller expression seems to be svajāti-lakṣaṇa, see <ls>Laṅk</ls> 〔38.16 ff.〕, <ab>esp.</ab> 〔18 f.〕, svajātilakṣaṇe punar nirudhyamāne (<ab>mss.</ab>) ālayavijñānanirodhaḥ syāt, suggesting that with its suppression, the ālaya-vijñāna itself is suppressed; for the aṣṭalakṣaṇa {@vijñāna@} see {@vij°@} 2; ({@2@}) in <ls>Divy</ls> 〔513.15, 24〕, sauvarṇena lakṣaṇena laḍḍīś (<ab>sc.</ab> of a state horse) chorayati, {%removes the dung with a golden …%} (? some sort of implement; <ab>acc.</ab> to Index, {%spoon?%}), <ab>perh.</ab> {%shovel%} or the like; ({@3@}) = {@svabhāva@} (2), <ab>q.v.</ab>, {%characteristic%}, of existing things, there being three such, <ab>viz.</ab> {@parikalpita, paratantra, pariniṣpanna@}, <ab>qq.v.</ab>: <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔1662〕 (to 〔1665〕 <ab>incl.</ab>); <ls>Sūtrāl.</ls> 〔xi.38—41〕 (<ls>Lévi</ls>, {%indice%}); svabhāva-lakṣaṇa-trayakuśalena bhavitavyam <ls>Laṅk</ls> 〔67.2〕; ({@4@}) {%characteristic mark%} of a superior person (a cakravartin or a Buddha), of which there are standardly 32 (anomalously 28 in <ls>Gv</ls> 〔353.7〕, aṣṭaviṃśatibhir mahāpuruṣalakṣaṇair upeto; no list). There are various lists; in <lang>Pali</lang> (lakkhaṇa), <ls>DN</ls> 〔ii.17.10 ff.〕 and 〔iii.143.5 ff.〕 (here followed by lengthy treatments of each item); <ls>MN</ls> 〔ii.136.6 ff.〕; in <lang>BHS</lang>, <ls>LV</ls> 〔105.11 ff.〕 [Page458-1b] (here referred to as <ls>LVa</ls>) and 〔429.3 ff.〕 (<ls>LVb</ls>); <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔235 ff.〕; <ls>Dharmas</ls> (here abbreviated <ls>Dh</ls>) 83; <ls>Gv</ls> 〔399.20 ff.〕, with valuable brief explanations of each term; <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔375.9 ff.〕, with a few brief glosses, but followed on 〔378.3 ff., 381.8 ff.〕, by more extensive treatments of the various items, with a few minor variants which are mostly not recorded here; finally, <ls>Mv</ls> 〔i.226.16 ff.〕 = 〔ii.29.19 ff.〕 has, in 7 lines of verse, extremely brief one-word designations for the 32 items, in part so corrupt in the text that I have failed to identify a few items (here, <ls>Mv</ls> without reference refers to this list); again, <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.304.14 ff.〕 has a very loose, inaccurate, and incomplete list, mingled with some {@anuvyañjana@} and other extraneous materials; this is cited below by page and line when it is important. Finally, a few stray lakṣaṇa are unsystematically mentioned in <ls>RP</ls> 〔46.13—47.12〕, and again 〔50.11—51.5〕; they will be referred to by page and line under the appropriate items. In modern literature, correlations of various <lang>Pali</lang> and <lang>BHS</lang> lists (but without the <ls>Gv</ls>, <ls>Bbh</ls>, and <ls>Mv</ls> lists) have been recorded by <ls>Burnouf, Lotus</ls>, 〔558 ff.〕; <ls>Müller, note on Dharmas</ls> 〔83〕 (but note that in a number of cases <ls>Müller</ls> here cites <ls>Dharmas</ls> itself inconsistently with his own text). In <ls>Mvy</ls> and <ls>LVa</ls> (as also in the stray fragmentary lists of <ls>RP</ls>) the order of all other texts is reversed, so as to begin with the head instead of the feet; in citing numbers I have reversed the numbering of these two lists, to facilitate comparison with the other lists; therefore when I cite ‘<ls>Mvy</ls> 〔32〕, <ls>LVa</ls> 〔32〕’, I refer to <ls>Mvy</ls> and <ls>LVa</ls> 〔1〕; ‘<ls>Mvy</ls> 〔31〕, <ls>LVa</ls> 〔31〕’ means <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔2〕, <ls>LVa</ls> 〔2〕, <ab>etc.</ab> I believe the following list is substantially correct and original, <ab>tho</ab> the precise language is not always certain; all important variants are cited. The order of the items in <lang>BHS</lang> varies greatly, no two lists being alike; but the relative order in the <lang>Pali</lang> lists is, I believe, always or nearly always supported by some <lang>BHS</lang> evidence, and I see no serious reason to doubt that it represents the original; it is therefore adopted here. {@1@}. supratiṣṭhitapāda (<lang>Pali</lang> suppatiṭṭhitapāda), <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔3〕; [Page459-a] <ls>LVb</ls>, <ls>Gv</ls>, <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔1〕; <ls>LVa</ls> 〔1〕 inserts sama before pāda; <ls>Mv</ls> <ab>prob.</ab> means this by 1 samā; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.304.14〕 samā … caraṇā supratiṣṭhitā; <ls>Dh.</ls> 〔2〕 -pāṇipādatala(tā) for -pāda. —{@2@}. adhastāt pādatalayoś cakre jāte … (epithets), so <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔2〕, similarly <ls>LVa</ls>, <ls>Gv</ls> 〔2〕; <lang>Pali</lang> heṭṭhāpādatalesu cakkāni jātāni … (epithets); <ls>Mv</ls> 〔2〕 heṣṭā, also heṣṭā … <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.304.16〕; <ls>LVb</ls> 〔2〕 compresses the epithets into a long <ab>cpd.</ab> ending cakrāṅkitapādatala; <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔4〕 cakrāṅkita-hasta-pāda, and so <ls>Dh.</ls> 〔1〕 adding -tala and with pāṇi for hasta, which, <ab>tho</ab> supported by <lang>Tib.</lang> <tib>phyag</tib>, is only a false interpretation of adhastāt or semi-<lang>MIndic</lang> heṣṭā. —{@3@}. āyatapādapārṣṇi (<lang>Pali</lang> āyatapaṇhi), so <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔2〕, <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔4〕, <ls>Gv</ls> 〔5〕 (<ls>LVa</ls> 〔6〕 āyatapārṣṇipāda); or āyatapārṣṇi, <ls>LVb</ls> 〔3〕, <ls>Dh.</ls> 〔7〕, with <lang>Pali</lang>; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔4〕 āyatā. —{@4@}. dīrghāṅguli (<lang>Pali</lang> dīgha°), <ls>LVb</ls> 〔4〕, <ls>LVa</ls> 〔7〕, <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔5〕, <ls>Dh.</ls> 〔6〕, <ls>Gv</ls> (<ed>2d ed.</ed>) 6 dīrghā asyāṅgulayo, <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔3〕; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔3〕 dīrghā; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.305.1〕. —{@5@}. mṛdutaruṇahastapāda (<lang>Pali</lang> mudutaluṇahatthapāda); <ls>LVa</ls> 〔4〕, <ls>LVb</ls> 〔6〕; <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔5〕 (<ab>mss.</ab> <ab>om.</ab> hasta, <lang>Tib.</lang> <tib>phyag</tib>, for which <ab>ed.</ab> pāṇi); <ls>Dh.</ls> 〔4〕 and <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔7〕 add -tala; <ls>Gv</ls> 〔7〕 mṛdūni … hastapādatalāni; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔11〕 mṛdu; <ab>cf.</ab> <ls>RP</ls> 〔47.10〕. —{@6@}. jāla-(jālāvanaddha-?)hastapāda; <lang>Pali</lang> jālahatthapāda, to which <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔6〕 jālapāṇipāda is closest; References to the 32 lakṣaṇa, usually as seen on a Buddha, are frequent, <ab>e.g.</ab> <ls>SP</ls> 〔47.10〕; and see <ab>s.v.</ab> {@lakṣa@} for two cases where <ls>Senart</ls> assumes, wrongly I think, that <ls>Mv</ls> substitutes that word for lakṣaṇa.
;
51753 new {@lakṣaṇa@}¦, <lex>nt.</lex>, {%mark%} (<lang>Skt.</lang>); ({@1@}) in <ls>Laṅk</ls> 〔37.10 ff.〕; 〔38.5 ff.〕, {%external mark, manifested aspect%}, of the vijñāna (<ab>cf.</ab> <ls>Suzuki, Studies</ls>, 〔183〕); contrasted with {@prabandha@}, <ab>q.v.</ab>; fuller expression seems to be svajāti-lakṣaṇa, see <ls>Laṅk</ls> 〔38.16 ff.〕, <ab>esp.</ab> 〔18 f.〕, svajātilakṣaṇe punar nirudhyamāne (<ab>mss.</ab>) ālayavijñānanirodhaḥ syāt, suggesting that with its suppression, the ālaya-vijñāna itself is suppressed; for the aṣṭalakṣaṇa {@vijñāna@} see {@vij°@} 2; ({@2@}) in <ls>Divy</ls> 〔513.15, 24〕, sauvarṇena lakṣaṇena laḍḍīś (<ab>sc.</ab> of a state horse) chorayati, {%removes the dung with a golden …%} (? some sort of implement; <ab>acc.</ab> to Index, {%spoon?%}), <ab>perh.</ab> {%shovel%} or the like; ({@3@}) = {@svabhāva@} (2), <ab>q.v.</ab>, {%characteristic%}, of existing things, there being three such, <ab>viz.</ab> {@parikalpita, paratantra, pariniṣpanna@}, <ab>qq.v.</ab>: <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔1662〕 (to 〔1665〕 <ab>incl.</ab>); <ls>Sūtrāl.</ls> 〔xi.38—41〕 (<ls>Lévi</ls>, {%<fr>indice</fr>%}); svabhāva-lakṣaṇa-trayakuśalena bhavitavyam <ls>Laṅk</ls> 〔67.2〕; ({@4@}) {%characteristic mark%} of a superior person (a cakravartin or a Buddha), of which there are standardly 32 (anomalously 28 in <ls>Gv</ls> 〔353.7〕, aṣṭaviṃśatibhir mahāpuruṣalakṣaṇair upeto; no list). There are various lists; in <lang>Pali</lang> (lakkhaṇa), <ls>DN</ls> 〔ii.17.10 ff.〕 and 〔iii.143.5 ff.〕 (here followed by lengthy treatments of each item); <ls>MN</ls> 〔ii.136.6 ff.〕; in <lang>BHS</lang>, <ls>LV</ls> 〔105.11 ff.〕 [Page458-1b] (here referred to as <ls>LVa</ls>) and 〔429.3 ff.〕 (<ls>LVb</ls>); <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔235 ff.〕; <ls>Dharmas</ls> (here abbreviated <ls>Dh</ls>) 83; <ls>Gv</ls> 〔399.20 ff.〕, with valuable brief explanations of each term; <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔375.9 ff.〕, with a few brief glosses, but followed on 〔378.3 ff., 381.8 ff.〕, by more extensive treatments of the various items, with a few minor variants which are mostly not recorded here; finally, <ls>Mv</ls> 〔i.226.16 ff.〕 = 〔ii.29.19 ff.〕 has, in 7 lines of verse, extremely brief one-word designations for the 32 items, in part so corrupt in the text that I have failed to identify a few items (here, <ls>Mv</ls> without reference refers to this list); again, <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.304.14 ff.〕 has a very loose, inaccurate, and incomplete list, mingled with some {@anuvyañjana@} and other extraneous materials; this is cited below by page and line when it is important. Finally, a few stray lakṣaṇa are unsystematically mentioned in <ls>RP</ls> 〔46.13—47.12〕, and again 〔50.11—51.5〕; they will be referred to by page and line under the appropriate items. In modern literature, correlations of various <lang>Pali</lang> and <lang>BHS</lang> lists (but without the <ls>Gv</ls>, <ls>Bbh</ls>, and <ls>Mv</ls> lists) have been recorded by <ls>Burnouf, Lotus</ls>, 〔558 ff.〕; <ls>Müller, note on Dharmas</ls> 〔83〕 (but note that in a number of cases <ls>Müller</ls> here cites <ls>Dharmas</ls> itself inconsistently with his own text). In <ls>Mvy</ls> and <ls>LVa</ls> (as also in the stray fragmentary lists of <ls>RP</ls>) the order of all other texts is reversed, so as to begin with the head instead of the feet; in citing numbers I have reversed the numbering of these two lists, to facilitate comparison with the other lists; therefore when I cite ‘<ls>Mvy</ls> 〔32〕, <ls>LVa</ls> 〔32〕’, I refer to <ls>Mvy</ls> and <ls>LVa</ls> 〔1〕; ‘<ls>Mvy</ls> 〔31〕, <ls>LVa</ls> 〔31〕’ means <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔2〕, <ls>LVa</ls> 〔2〕, <ab>etc.</ab> I believe the following list is substantially correct and original, <ab>tho</ab> the precise language is not always certain; all important variants are cited. The order of the items in <lang>BHS</lang> varies greatly, no two lists being alike; but the relative order in the <lang>Pali</lang> lists is, I believe, always or nearly always supported by some <lang>BHS</lang> evidence, and I see no serious reason to doubt that it represents the original; it is therefore adopted here. {@1@}. supratiṣṭhitapāda (<lang>Pali</lang> suppatiṭṭhitapāda), <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔3〕; [Page459-a] <ls>LVb</ls>, <ls>Gv</ls>, <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔1〕; <ls>LVa</ls> 〔1〕 inserts sama before pāda; <ls>Mv</ls> <ab>prob.</ab> means this by 1 samā; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.304.14〕 samā … caraṇā supratiṣṭhitā; <ls>Dh.</ls> 〔2〕 -pāṇipādatala(tā) for -pāda. —{@2@}. adhastāt pādatalayoś cakre jāte … (epithets), so <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔2〕, similarly <ls>LVa</ls>, <ls>Gv</ls> 〔2〕; <lang>Pali</lang> heṭṭhāpādatalesu cakkāni jātāni … (epithets); <ls>Mv</ls> 〔2〕 heṣṭā, also heṣṭā … <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.304.16〕; <ls>LVb</ls> 〔2〕 compresses the epithets into a long <ab>cpd.</ab> ending cakrāṅkitapādatala; <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔4〕 cakrāṅkita-hasta-pāda, and so <ls>Dh.</ls> 〔1〕 adding -tala and with pāṇi for hasta, which, <ab>tho</ab> supported by <lang>Tib.</lang> <tib>phyag</tib>, is only a false interpretation of adhastāt or semi-<lang>MIndic</lang> heṣṭā. —{@3@}. āyatapādapārṣṇi (<lang>Pali</lang> āyatapaṇhi), so <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔2〕, <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔4〕, <ls>Gv</ls> 〔5〕 (<ls>LVa</ls> 〔6〕 āyatapārṣṇipāda); or āyatapārṣṇi, <ls>LVb</ls> 〔3〕, <ls>Dh.</ls> 〔7〕, with <lang>Pali</lang>; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔4〕 āyatā. —{@4@}. dīrghāṅguli (<lang>Pali</lang> dīgha°), <ls>LVb</ls> 〔4〕, <ls>LVa</ls> 〔7〕, <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔5〕, <ls>Dh.</ls> 〔6〕, <ls>Gv</ls> (<ed>2d ed.</ed>) 6 dīrghā asyāṅgulayo, <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔3〕; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔3〕 dīrghā; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.305.1〕. —{@5@}. mṛdutaruṇahastapāda (<lang>Pali</lang> mudutaluṇahatthapāda); <ls>LVa</ls> 〔4〕, <ls>LVb</ls> 〔6〕; <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔5〕 (<ab>mss.</ab> <ab>om.</ab> hasta, <lang>Tib.</lang> <tib>phyag</tib>, for which <ab>ed.</ab> pāṇi); <ls>Dh.</ls> 〔4〕 and <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔7〕 add -tala; <ls>Gv</ls> 〔7〕 mṛdūni … hastapādatalāni; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔11〕 mṛdu; <ab>cf.</ab> <ls>RP</ls> 〔47.10〕. —{@6@}. jāla-(jālāvanaddha-?)hastapāda; <lang>Pali</lang> jālahatthapāda, to which <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔6〕 jālapāṇipāda is closest; <ls>LVa</ls> 〔3〕, <ls>LVb</ls> 〔7〕 jālāṅgulihastapāda; <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔6〕 jālāvanaddha-hastapāda, <ab>cf.</ab> <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.304.14〕 (combined with 〔No. 1〕 above) jālāvanaddhā (caraṇā); <ls>Dh.</ls> 〔3〕 corrupt, jālābalabaddhāṅgulipāṇipādatala(tā); <ls>Gv</ls> 〔4〕 hastapādatale jālinī (<ed>2d ed.</ed>); <ls>Mv</ls> 〔12〕 jālā. —{@7@}. ucchaṅkha-(?)pāda (<lang>Pali</lang> ussaṅkha°), so <ls>Gv</ls> 〔3〕, and so read (ucchaṅkha) <ls>Mv</ls> 〔5〕 and <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.304.19〕, also with <ls>Mironov</ls> <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔8〕; <ls>Mvy</ls> <ed>Kyoto ed.</ed> utsaṅga°, so <ls>LVa</ls> 〔5〕, <ls>Dh.</ls> 〔9〕, and <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔7〕 (-caraṇa for pāda); <ls>LVb</ls> 〔8〕 ucchaṅga°. —{@8@}. aiṇeyajaṅgha (<lang>Pali</lang> eṇi-j°), so <ls>Gv</ls> 〔8〕, <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔1〕, <ls>Dh.</ls> 〔11〕; eṇeya° <ls>LVb</ls> 〔10〕, <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔8〕 (and <ls>RP</ls> 〔51.3〕); eṇeyamṛgarājajaṅgha <ls>LVa</ls> 〔8〕; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔6〕 eṇi; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.305.3〕 eṇī-j°; <ls>RP</ls> 〔47.12〕 eṇajaṅgha. —{@9@}. sthitānavanata-pralambabāhu <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔15〕, and sthito'vanata° (as <ls>Mvy</ls>) <ls>LVa</ls> 〔15〕; <ls>Mv</ls>(?); <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.305.8〕 anonatena kāyena pāṇīhi jānukāṃ spṛśe; <ab>cf.</ab> <ls>RP</ls> 〔47.9〕 dīrgha-parigha-bāhū. —{@10@}. kośopagata-vastiguhya (<lang>Pali</lang> kosohitavatthaguyha; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.305.14〕 and <ls>RP</ls> 〔51.5〕 ślakṣṇachavī. —{@13@}. ekaikaroma (or °man; <lang>Pali</lang> ekekaloma), so <ls>LVa</ls> 〔12〕; <ls>Gv</ls> 〔30〕; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.305.15〕; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔14〕 ekā; <ls>Dh.</ls> 〔17〕 ūrṇālaṃkṛtamukhatā; <ls>Gv</ls> 〔26〕 bhruvāntare … ūrṇā jātābhūn mṛdvī … śuddhā prabhāsvarā himaguḍikā-tuṣāravarṇā …; <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔32〕 ūrṇā … bhruvor madhye jātā śvetā śaṅkhasaṃnibhā pradakṣiṇāvartā (<ab>cf.</ab> <ls>LV</ls>, <ls>Mvy</ls>); <ls>LVa</ls> 〔31〕 (<ab>cf.</ab> <ls>LVb</ls> below, <ls>LVa</ls> 〔29〕 above, <ls>Bbh</ls>, and <ls>Mvy</ls>) … pradakṣināvartakeśaḥ; [Page460-a] <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔29〕 ūrṇākośaḥ (so read), and 31 pradakṣiṇāvartakeśaḥ; <ls>LVb</ls> 〔31〕 bhrūmadhye-sujātapradakṣiṇāvartottaptaviśuddhavarṇābhāsorṇa(ḥ, <ab>n. sg.</ab>, <ab>Bhvr.</ab>); <ls>Mv</ls> 〔31〕 ūrṇā. <ab>Cf.</ab> <ls>RP</ls> 〔46.14〕; 〔50.12〕. —{@32@}. uṣṇīṣaśīrṣa (see <ab>s.v.</ab> {@uṣṇīṣa@}; <lang>Pali</lang> uṇhīsasīsa), <ls>LVa</ls> 〔32〕; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔32〕; <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.307.4〕; <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔31〕 (°ṣāḥ); °śiraska(-tā) <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔32〕; <ls>Dh</ls> 〔23〕; mūrdhni … uṣṇīṣam <ls>Gv</ls> 〔27〕; uṣṇīṣaśīrṣānavalokitamūrdha <ls>LVb</ls> 〔30〕; uṣṇi <ls>RP</ls> 〔46.13〕; 〔50.11〕. —A few secondary insertions in individual lists are here ignored. References to the 32 lakṣaṇa, usually as seen on a Buddha, are frequent, <ab>e.g.</ab> <ls>SP</ls> 〔47.10〕; and see <ab>s.v.</ab> {@lakṣa@} for two cases where <ls>Senart</ls> assumes, wrongly I think, that <ls>Mv</ls> substitutes that word for lakṣaṇa.

; <L>13069<pc>464,1<k1>lokAntarikA<k2>lokAntarikA

;52433 old {@lokāntarikā@}¦, <lex>subst.</lex> <lex>f.</lex>, usually <ab>pl.</ab> (= <lang>Pali</lang> lokantarikā, [Page464-b] <lex>subst.</lex>, not <lex>adj.</lex>, ‘<ab>scil.</ab> Niraya’, with <ls>PTSD</ls>), {%interstice(s) between the worlds%}; they are dark, gloomy places, a kind of purgatories: chiefly in a well-known cliché, recorded <ls>SP</ls> 〔163.8〕; <ls>LV</ls> 〔51.10〕; 〔410.13〕 (and the first part, ending andhakārās, as abbreviation, 〔351.22—352.1〕); <ls>Mv</ls> 〔i.41.4〕; 〔229.20〕; 〔240.9〕; 〔ii.162.9〕; 〔iii.334.7〕; 〔341.12〕; <ls>Divy</ls> 〔204.22〕; 〔205.4, 13, 23〕; 〔206.5, 16〕; <ls>Samādh</ls> page 7 line 9; <ls>ŚsP</ls> 〔102.17〕 (abbreviated); and in <lang>Pali</lang>, <ls>DN</ls> 〔ii.12.10〕; <ls>MN</ls> 〔iii.120.9〕; <ls>AN</ls> 〔ii.130.24〕; <ls>SN</ls> 〔v.454.16〕. There are minor variants <ab>thru</ab>out, not all reported here, and in <ls>Mv</ls> the <ab>mss.</ab> are mostly quite corrupt and vary widely; <ls>Senart</ls> <ab>em.</ab> rashly; I shall quote a blended version which seems at least close to a common <ls>Mv</ls> text. For convenience the passage is divided into sections, (a) to (g); <ls>Divy</ls> lacks (b) and (f); <ls>ŚsP</ls> lacks (a) and (g); in <ls>Samādh</ls>, (b) is lacking, (a) and (c) come after (f); in <ls>Mv</ls> (all six passages) and in <ls>ŚsP</ls>, (b) comes after (c): (a) <ab>om.</ab> <ls>ŚsP</ls>; yā (a)pi tā (<ls>Divy</ls> adds lokasya; 〔204.22〕 lacks api tā, and so also <ls>SP</ls>; 3 of 6 <ls>Mv</ls> passages add loke) lokāntarikā (<lang>Pali</lang> lokant°); (b) omitted in <ls>Divy</ls>, <ls>Samādh</ls>, and <ab>prob.</ab> corrupt in all; I believe <ab>orig.</ab> had aghā aghasaṃvṛtā (<lang>Pali</lang> aghā asaṃvutā, for which <ls>Senart</ls>, <ls>Mv</ls> 〔i.406〕, brilliantly conjectured aghā aghasaṃvutā; the <lang>Pali</lang> <ab>comms.</ab> seem to me fatuous, and I cannot feel attracted by <ls>CPD</ls>ʼs interpretation of aghā, see <ab>s.v.</ab> {@agha@}; <ls>Mv</ls> supports <ls>Senart</ls>, and so in a measure do <ls>SP</ls>, <ls>LV</ls> and <ls>ŚsP</ls>); the <ls>Mv</ls> tradition seems to point to aghā aghasaṃbhūtapūrvā, in which with <ls>Senart</ls> I regard saṃbhūta as a corruption for saṃvṛta, or <lang>MIndic</lang> saṃvuta; close in sense, also, is aghā aghasphuṭā ({%full of misery%}), the reading of <ls>LV</ls> and <ls>ŚsP</ls> (in <ls>ŚsP</ls> after c); finally, <ls>SP</ls>, <ab>tho</ab> substituting (tāsu ya) akṣaṇāḥ for the first aghā, and omitting the 2d agha-, actually preserves saṃvṛtā(ḥ), alone among <lang>BHS</lang> texts (note that it has no negative! thus tending to show the corruption of the <lang>Pali</lang>); (c) andhakārā andhakāratamisrā(ḥ) (<lang>Pali</lang> andhakārā andhakāratimisā); so <ls>Samādh</ls>; <ls>SP</ls> <ab>ed.</ab> omits andhakārā (<ab>haplogr.</ab>), but <ab>v.l.</ab> has it; either it or andhakāra- is omitted in <ls>ŚsP</ls> and both <ls>LV</ls> versions (<ab>haplogr.</ab>); <ls>Divy</ls> andhās tamaso 'ndhakāratamisrā; <ls>Mv</ls> (very confused) seems <ab>orig.</ab> to have read, andhakārā andhakārāpitatvā (or °rāyitatvā) tamisrā (or ti°) tamisrāyitatvā (or ti°); (d) yatremāu (yatra ime, <ab>etc.</ab>) candrasūryā(v; or variants) evaṃ maharddhikā(v) (sometimes omitted) evaṃ mahānubhāvā(v); <ls>SP</ls>, <ls>LV</ls>, <ls>ŚsP</ls>, <ls>Samādh</ls> add other adjectives <ab>prec.</ab> by evaṃ; <lang>Pali</lang> yattha p'ime candimasuriyā evaṃ mahiddhikā evaṃ mahānubhāvā; (e) ābhayā (or ābhāya, <ab>etc.</ab>, <ls>Mv</ls>; <lang>Pali</lang> ābhāya) ābhāṃ (or ābhāsaṃ; <ab>om.</ab> <lang>Pali</lang>) nānubhavanti (so <ab>prob.</ab> <ab>orig.</ab>; <ls>LV</ls> <ab>om.</ab> nānu°; <lang>Pali</lang> nānubhonti, but <ls>SP</ls> nānubhavataḥ, <ls>Divy</ls> na pratyanubhavataḥ, <ls>ŚsP</ls> and <ls>Samādh</ls> na bhāsato, omitting ābhayā ābhāṃ before it; <ls>Mv</ls> clearly intends nābhisaṃbhuṇanti, all 6 times; <lang>Pali</lang> <ab>comm.</ab> on <ls>DN</ls>, 〔ii.433.23〕, attano pabhāya na-ppahonti, on which the ‘old ṭīkā’ cited <ls>CPD</ls> glosses … obhāsituṃ an-abhisaṃbhuṇanti, <ab>cf.</ab> <ls>Mv</ls>!); (f) ? not in <lang>Pali</lang> or <ls>Divy</ls>, <ab>perh.</ab> not <ab>orig.</ab>; <ls>SP</ls> varṇenāpi varṇaṃ tejasāpi tejo nānubhavataḥ; <ls>LV</ls> varṇena varṇaṃ tejasā tejo nābhitapato nābhivirocataḥ (best <ab>mss.</ab> nāti° for nābhi° both times); <ls>ŚsP</ls>, <ls>Samādh</ls>, na tapato na virocataḥ; <ls>Mv</ls> ālokena vā ālokaṃ na spharanti; (g) uncertain; not in <ls>ŚsP</ls>; <lang>Pali</lang> tattha pi appamāṇo uḷāro obhāso pātubhavati; <ls>SP</ls>, <ls>LV</ls> (in <ls>LV</ls> after insertion) tatrāpi (<ls>SP</ls> tāsv api) tasmin samaye mahata udārasyāvabhāsasya (<ls>SP</ls> mahato 'vabhāsasya) prādurbhāvo 'bhūt; <ls>Divy</ls> tā api tasmin samaye udāreṇāvabhāsena sphuṭā bhavanti; <ls>Samādh</ls> tā api tasmin samaye tenāvabhāsena sphuṭā abhūvan; <ls>Mv</ls> te (once tā) pi tena obhāsena sphuṭā abhūnsuḥ, with <ab>varr.</ab> The entire cliché means approximately: {%And even those world-interstitial-spaces%}, (which are) {%miseries and covered over with miseries, darknesses, glooms of darkness, —in which the moon and sun here, which possess such great supernatural power and dignity%} (or {%capacity%}), {%are not capable of%} (producing) {%light by%} (their) [Page465-a] {%light, …%} (f varies too much to admit a unified rendering,) {%even in them a great, magnificent radiance appeared (at that time)%}. —Besides this cliché, lokāntarikā occurs in, na ca vedayanti duḥkhaṃ °rikā vipadyamānā (? <ab>em.</ab>) <ls>Mv</ls> 〔ii.34.16〕; alone, <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔3062〕; lokadhātor °rikā duratikramā <ls>Dbh</ls> 〔58.11〕; sarva-°rikāś ca tasmin samaye mahatāvabhāsena sphuṭā abhūvan <ls>LV</ls> 〔86.19〕 (<ab>cf.</ab> the cliché, g); (na ca bhūyo) °rikā … prajñāyante sma <ls>LV</ls> 〔277.9〕.
;

54471 old {@vāsī-candana-kalpa@}¦, <lex>adj.</lex> (= <lang>AMg.</lang> vāsī-candaṇakappa, see below), a stock <ab>ep.</ab> of an arhat; in effect, {%indifferent%}; only in a cliché list of such epithets, always following (and in every case but one immediately) samaloṣṭakāñcana and ākāśapāṇitalasamacitta, with other similar terms: <ls>Divy</ls> 〔97.26〕; 〔180.26〕 (here <ab>v.l.</ab> vālī°); 〔240.25〕; 〔282.2〕; 〔551.19〕; <ls>MSV</ls> 〔ii.131.3〕; <ls>Av</ls> 〔i.96.7〕 (<ab>ms.</ab>); 〔104.7〕; 〔207.12〕, <ab>etc.</ab>; <ab>acc.</ab> to <ls>Ratnach.</ls>, {%indifferent alike to being cut with a hatchet%} (<lang>Skt.</lang> vāśī, also written vāsī) {%or anointed with sandalwood paste%}; this is clearly the Jain traditional interpretation, misunderstood by <ls>Jacobi, SBE 45</ls>, 〔p. 99, note 1〕; in <ls>transl. of Kalpa Sūtra</ls> 〔119〕 <ls>Jacobi</ls> renders vāsī by [Page479-b] {%ordure%}, and Charpentier on <ls>Uttarādh.</ls> 〔19.92〕 also thinks it means something ill-smelling, in contrast with sandal; they both agree with the Jain tradition in understanding kalpa as {%indifferent to%} (pairs of opposites, like <lang>Skt.</lang> sama); perhaps this is right, but if so I know of no parallel for it; ordinary usage, both <lang>Skt.</lang> and <lang>MIndic</lang>, would make it mean {%like, resembling …%}; in this case, possibly, {%resembling a knife or sandalwood%} in ‘coldness’, dispassionate nature?. So in effect <ls>Feer, Av transl.</ls> 〔p. 14〕, {%<fr>il était devenu froid comme le sandal</fr>%}; but <ls>Feer</ls> omits vāsī!

LaV-P.</ls> 〔ii.239〕 by {%<fr>akṣara, <fr>phonème</fr> (varṇa), <fr>voyelle et consonne, par exemple</fr> a, ā, i, ī, <ab>etc.</ab></fr>%}; here and in °na-kāyaḥ (see {@kāya@} 2) <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔1997〕 contrasted with {@nāman@}, {%word%}, and {@pada@}, {%sentence%}; much more commonly in contrast with artha, {%meaning%}, and regularly in such a context with implication of the {%‘letter’%} as against the {%‘spirit’%} (artha, the real {%meaning%}) in a sense close to the Biblical usage: arthato vā °nato vā <ls>SP</ls> 〔200.6〕, {%either in regard to the meaning (spirit) or the letter%} (<lang>Pali</lang> also atthato vā °nato vā); in <ls>Sūtrāl.</ls> 〔xviii.32〕, <ab>comm.</ab>, vyañjanasya is equated with yathārutārthasya, see <ab>s.v.</ab> {@ruta@} (2); na vyañjanā (<ab>v.l.</ab> °naṃ) bhrasyati (= bhraś°) nāpi cārthā <ls>LV</ls> 〔444.8〕 (<ab>vs</ab>), {%neither sound(s) nor sense is lost%}; (saddharmaṃ …) svarthaṃ suvyañjanaṃ <ls>LV</ls> 〔3.8〕, {%having good meaning and good sound(s)%}; arthena mahyaṃ kāriyaṃ kiṃ bhoti vyañjanaṃ subahukaṃ <ls>Mv</ls> 〔iii.60.20〕 (<ab>vs</ab>; so <ab>mss.</ab>, with <ab>varr.</ab>; corrupt, but <ab>prob.</ab> was an āryā line), {%my concern is with the meaning, what is the use of abundant sound ?%}; artha-pratisaraṇa as against vyañjana-prati°, <ls>Mvy</ls> 〔1546〕, <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔175.16〕, see <ab>s.v.</ab> {@pratisaraṇa@} (1); na vyañjanābhisaṃskārārthī, saḥ arthārthī … na vyañjanārthī <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔256.25〕; śāstuḥ śrāvakāṇāṃ cārthenārthaḥ padena padaṃ ({%word%}, or {%sentence?%} see <ab>s.v.</ab>) vyañjanena vyañjanaṃ saṃsyandate sameti yad utāgrapadaiḥ <ls>Av</ls> 〔ii.142.16〕; 〔143.5—6〕; pada-vyañjanaṃ, dvandva or <ab>tatp.</ab> ? ;66513 old {@sahadhārmika@}¦, <lex>adj.</lex> (to <ab>prec.</ab>, <ab>q.v.</ab>, plus -ika; = <lang>Pali</lang> sahadhammika, which in the <ab>Dictt.</ab> is sometimes assigned this <ab>mg.</ab>, sometimes defined {%co-religionist%}, a <ab>mg.</ab> which need, and <ab>prob.</ab> should, never be assumed in <lang>BHS</lang>, nor, I suspect, in <lang>Pali</lang>), {%consonant with the%} (true) {%Doctrine%}; <lex>m.</lex>, of a person, {%one who lives in consonance therewith%} (the <ab>mg.</ab> {%having the same doctrine%} is given by <ls>Wogihara</ls>ʼs <lang>Chin.</lang> renderings in <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔Index〕 but is never necessary and sometimes impossible): °ke dharmaśravaṇe <ls>Śikṣ</ls> 〔55.6〕; °keno (<ab>m.c.</ab> for °kena) vacanena 〔194.7〕 (<ab>vs</ab>), <ab>cf.</ab> <lang>Pali</lang> sahadhammiko vādānuvādo <ls>Vin.</ls> 〔i.234.19—20〕, °ke vuccamāne <ls>Dhs.</ls> 〔1327〕; personal, yā ca °kasya darśanenābhipramodanā <ls>Bbh</ls> 〔30.11〕, {%joy at sight of one who is true to the Doctrine%}; °kaṃ ca dṛṣṭvā sumanā bhavati 〔184.26〕; (bodhisattvo vṛddhatarakaṃ guṇavantaṃ …) °kaṃ dṛṣṭvā 〔161.12〕; °kasya bodhisattvasya kṛtapraṇidhānatayā 〔152.24〕, {%because a Bodhisattva that is consistent with the doctrine has%} (must necessarily have) {%made an ‘earnest wish’ (vow for enlightenment)%}; in the last the alleged meaning {%co-religionist%} is peculiarly impossible, but nevertheless given by <ls>Wogihara</ls>ʼs <lang>Chin.</lang> ({%of the same Doctrine%}). On the <lang>Pali</lang> <ab>mg.</ab> see <ab>esp.</ab> Mahāniddesa 〔485.16〕 (a gloss on <ls>Sn</ls> 〔965〕) paradhammikā vuccanti satta sahadhammike ṭhapetvā ye keci Buddhe appasannā … (also dhamme, saṃghe), te bhikkhū <ab>etc.</ab>; note that even the paradhammikā here are {%monks%}, but have no faith in the Buddha <ab>etc.</ab>; in contrast the sahadhammikā (of seven sorts; which seven?) are {%in accord with the true doctrine%}.
;
